%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Small-\texorpdfstring{$p$}{p} Drift Control for the Minimal Same-Shell Non-Enriched Slot}

\section{Short explanation}

The practical route for the same-shell non-enriched benchmark is already fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the finite Hermitian matrix \(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0)\);
\item verify that its spectrum avoids zero at \(p=0\);
\item bound the \(p\)-dependent perturbation uniformly on \(|p|\le \rho\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the final benchmark-side issue is not conceptual.
It is the explicit control of the small-\(p\) drift
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)-H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0).
\]

\section{1. Minimal \(m=1\) block}

For the minimal same-shell non-enriched truncation \(N=1\), the block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:sp_block}
\end{equation}

Near \(p=0\), expand
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_\pm(p)=d_\pm^{(0)}+p_i a_{\pm,i}+R_\pm^{(2)}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p),
}
\label{eq:sp_expand}
\end{equation}
where
\[
R_\pm^{(2)}(p)=O(|p|^2),
\qquad
R_m^{(2)}(p)=O(|p|^2).
\]

Define the zero-momentum block
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_0^{(1)}
:=
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+^{(0)} & m_0\\
\overline{m_0} & d_-^{(0)}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:sp_H0}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_0^{(1)}
:=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_0^{(1)})\bigr).
}
\label{eq:sp_Delta0}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Uniform perturbation reduction}

Write
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)=H_0^{(1)}+\delta H^{(1)}(p),
\]
where
\[
\delta H^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
p_i a_{+,i}+R_+^{(2)}(p) & p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p)\\
\overline{p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p)} & p_i a_{-,i}+R_-^{(2)}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Define the uniform small-\(p\) drift budget
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H^{(1)}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:sp_eps_def}
\end{equation}

By the same Hermitian perturbation lemma used in the finite-to-exact upgrade,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\ge
\Delta_0^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:sp_gap_upgrade}
\end{equation}

Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}<\Delta_0^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:sp_positive_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0.
}
\label{eq:sp_positive_gap}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Explicit norm bound for the drift}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i |a_{+,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
A_-
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i |a_{-,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
B
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i |b_i|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:sp_ABC}
\end{equation}

Then for \(|p|\le \rho\),
\[
|p_i a_{+,i}|\le \rho A_+,
\qquad
|p_i a_{-,i}|\le \rho A_-,
\qquad
|p_i b_i|\le \rho B.
\]

Assume the quadratic remainders satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|R_+^{(2)}(p)|\le C_+\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_-^{(2)}(p)|\le C_-\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_m^{(2)}(p)|\le C_m\rho^2
\quad
(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:sp_Cbounds}
\end{equation}
for some finite constants \(C_\pm,C_m\).

Then, using the Frobenius norm as an upper bound on the operator norm,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:sp_eps_bound}
\end{equation}

At leading order in \(\rho\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
=
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+O(\rho^2),
\qquad
L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}
:=
\sqrt{A_+^2+A_-^2+2B^2}.
}
\label{eq:sp_leading}
\end{equation}

Thus a practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho\,L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}\rho^2
<
\Delta_0^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:sp_practical}
\end{equation}
for some finite quadratic constant \(C_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}\) absorbing \(C_\pm,C_m\).

\section{4. Zero-momentum gap in the explicit pure-even branch}

In the explicit branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
\]
the zero-momentum coefficients were reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+^{(0)}
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{++}^{EE},
\qquad
d_-^{(0)}
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{--}^{EE},
}
\label{eq:sp_d0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_0
=
B_{z_0}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE},
\qquad
a_K:=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\label{eq:sp_m0}
\end{equation}

If the residual is valley-symmetric,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}=\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}=:\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},
}
\label{eq:sp_sym}
\end{equation}
then
\[
d_+^{(0)}=d_-^{(0)}=:d^{(0)},
\]
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_0^{(1)}
=
\left|
\,|d^{(0)}|-|m_0|
\right|
=
\left|
\,
\left|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}\right|
-
\left|B_{z_0}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}\right|
\right|.
}
\label{eq:sp_Delta0_exact}
\end{equation}

A simpler sufficient lower bound is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_0^{(1)}
\ge
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|-2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},
}
\label{eq:sp_Delta0_simple}
\end{equation}
using \(|\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}|\le \mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}\).

\section{5. Final practical same-shell criterion}

Combining \eqref{eq:sp_gap_upgrade} and \eqref{eq:sp_Delta0_simple}, a sufficient practical criterion for the explicit branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:sp_master}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit bound \eqref{eq:sp_eps_bound}, one may impose the stronger but fully explicit inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:sp_master_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Minimal scalar-only locked core insertion}

In the minimal scalar-only locked core,
\[
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)=\omega_B(k_*)+12uA^2,
\qquad
B_{z_0}(0)=4uA^2,
\]
with
\[
\omega_B(k_*)
=
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}.
\]
Thus the practical same-shell criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:sp_scalar}
\end{equation}

If, moreover,
\[
u>0,
\qquad
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2\ge 0,
\]
this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+8uA^2
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:sp_scalar_simple}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Upgrade to the usable benchmark entry}

Finally, the exact usable same-shell entry is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
\]
So if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:sp_upgrade_cond}
\end{equation}
then the exact benchmark contribution is positive by the finite-to-exact upgrade theorem.

Therefore the complete same-shell non-enriched benchmark-side closure is reduced to the finite quantities
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\qquad
A_+,\qquad
A_-,\qquad
B,\qquad
C_+,\qquad
C_-,\qquad
C_m,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the minimal same-shell non-enriched truncation \(N=1\),
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Its uniform gap on \(|p|\le \rho\) is controlled by the zero-momentum gap and the small-\(p\) drift:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\ge
\Delta_0^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

If
\[
d_\pm(p)=d_\pm^{(0)}+p_i a_{\pm,i}+R_\pm^{(2)}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p),
\]
then with
\[
A_\pm=\Bigl(\sum_i |a_{\pm,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
B=\Bigl(\sum_i |b_i|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\]
one has the explicit bound
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\]

For the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
the practical same-shell sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)},
\qquad
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\]

In the minimal scalar-only locked core, this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Therefore the same-shell benchmark-side frontier is fully reduced to the finite constants
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\qquad
A_+,\qquad
A_-,\qquad
B,\qquad
C_+,\qquad
C_-,\qquad
C_m,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Small-\texorpdfstring{$p$}{p} Drift Coefficients for the Canonical Same-Shell Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

We now compute the derivative coefficients
\[
a_{+,i}=\partial_{p_i}d_+(0),
\qquad
a_{-,i}=\partial_{p_i}d_-(0),
\qquad
b_i=\partial_{p_i}m(0)
\]
for the explicit branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0.
\]

The key point is that the direct locked-core part is explicitly differentiable, while the pure-even \(KK\) residual contributes only through the momentum dependence of the overlap sums.
Thus the whole small-\(p\) drift is reduced to one explicit direct coefficient plus two finite residual derivative budgets.

\section{1. Same-shell coefficients in the explicit branch}

In the explicit pure-even residual branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_K\,\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p),
\qquad
d_-(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_K\,\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p),
}
\label{eq:drift_dpm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(p)=B_{z_0}(p)-a_K\,\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p),
\qquad
a_K:=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\label{eq:drift_m}
\end{equation}

Here the direct diagonal shell energy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)
=
\omega_B(k_*+p_\parallel \hat n + p_\perp)
+
12uA^2
+
[U^{(\mathrm{lock})}(0)]_{z_0z_0},
}
\label{eq:drift_Edir_p}
\end{equation}
while the direct opposite-valley Bragg term is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_{z_0}(p)=4uA^2+[U^{(\mathrm{lock})}(G_*)]_{z_0z_0}+O(|p|^2).
}
\label{eq:drift_Bp}
\end{equation}

The \(O(|p|^2)\) in \eqref{eq:drift_Bp} reflects the fact that the primitive Bragg Fourier coefficient is constant at leading shell order, so there is no linear direct off-diagonal drift.

\section{2. Direct core derivative coefficients}

The scalar direct core symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_B(k)
=
-\mu^2+Z|k|^2-Y|k|^4.
}
\label{eq:drift_omega}
\end{equation}
Hence
\[
\nabla_k\omega_B(k)=2Zk-4Y|k|^2k.
\]

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
|k_*|=\frac{q_*}{2},
\qquad
k_*= \frac{q_*}{2}\hat n,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\nabla_k\omega_B(k_*)
=
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\hat n.
}
\label{eq:drift_gradomega}
\end{equation}

Therefore the direct drift coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
}
\label{eq:drift_aplus_dir}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
}
\label{eq:drift_aminus_dir}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
}
\label{eq:drift_b_dir}
\end{equation}

So the direct same-shell drift is purely longitudinal and opposite in the two valley channels.

\section{3. Residual \(KK\) derivative coefficients}

Differentiate the overlap sums at \(p=0\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:drift_lpm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:drift_l0}
\end{equation}

Then the full derivative coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_K\,\ell_{+,i}^{EE},
}
\label{eq:drift_aplus_full}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_K\,\ell_{-,i}^{EE},
}
\label{eq:drift_aminus_full}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i
=
-a_K\,\ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
}
\label{eq:drift_b_full}
\end{equation}

Thus the residual derivative audit is reduced to the finite vectors
\[
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\qquad \ell_{-,i}^{EE},\qquad \ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
\]

\section{4. Norm-level drift constants}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0
:=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:drift_Lpm0}
\end{equation}

Then the drift magnitudes satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+
\le
\left|q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_K L_+,
}
\label{eq:drift_Aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-
\le
\left|q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_K L_-,
}
\label{eq:drift_Aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B\le a_K L_0.
}
\label{eq:drift_B}
\end{equation}

If the pure-even residual is valley-symmetric,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+=L_-=:L_{\mathrm{diag}},
}
\label{eq:drift_sym}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+=A_-\le
\left|q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_K L_{\mathrm{diag}},
\qquad
B\le a_K L_0.
}
\label{eq:drift_sym_bound}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final small-\(p\) budget}

Insert \eqref{eq:drift_Aplus}--\eqref{eq:drift_B} into the general drift estimate
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
\]
This gives the explicit practical bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Biggl[
\Bigl(
\rho\Bigl|q_*\bigl(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\bigr)\Bigr|
+
\rho a_K L_+
+
C_+\rho^2
\Bigr)^2
+
\Bigl(
\rho\Bigl|q_*\bigl(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\bigr)\Bigr|
+
\rho a_K L_-
+
C_-\rho^2
\Bigr)^2
+
2\bigl(\rho a_K L_0+C_m\rho^2\bigr)^2
\Biggr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:drift_eps_final}
\end{equation}

In the valley-symmetric subcase,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Biggl[
2\Bigl(
\rho\Bigl|q_*\bigl(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\bigr)\Bigr|
+
\rho a_K L_{\mathrm{diag}}
+
C_{\mathrm{diag}}\rho^2
\Bigr)^2
+
2\bigl(\rho a_K L_0+C_m\rho^2\bigr)^2
\Biggr]^{1/2},
}
\label{eq:drift_eps_sym}
\end{equation}
where \(C_{\mathrm{diag}}:=\max\{C_+,C_-\}\).

\section{6. Final practical same-shell inequality}

Combining the zero-momentum lower bound with the drift budget, a sufficient practical criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:drift_master}
\end{equation}

In the minimal scalar-only locked core,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:drift_master_scalar}
\end{equation}

So the entire same-shell benchmark-side frontier is reduced to the finite constants
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\qquad
L_+,\qquad
L_-,\qquad
L_0,\qquad
C_+,\qquad
C_-,\qquad
C_m.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
the same-shell non-enriched small-\(p\) drift is governed by
\[
a_{+,i}=\partial_{p_i}d_+(0),\qquad
a_{-,i}=\partial_{p_i}d_-(0),\qquad
b_i=\partial_{p_i}m(0).
\]

The direct locked-core contribution is completely explicit:
\[
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
}
\]

The full derivative coefficients are therefore
\[
\boxed{
a_{+,i}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-a_K\ell_{+,i}^{EE},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_{-,i}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-a_K\ell_{-,i}^{EE},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
b_i=-a_K\ell_{0,i}^{EE},
\qquad
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\]

Hence the drift magnitudes are controlled by the finite constants
\[
\boxed{
L_+
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\quad
L_-
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\quad
L_0
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\]

The explicit small-\(p\) budget is
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Biggl[
\Bigl(
\rho\Bigl|q_*\bigl(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\bigr)\Bigr|
+\rho a_K L_+
+C_+\rho^2
\Bigr)^2
+
\Bigl(
\rho\Bigl|q_*\bigl(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\bigr)\Bigr|
+\rho a_K L_-
+C_-\rho^2
\Bigr)^2
+
2(\rho a_K L_0+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Biggr]^{1/2}.
}
\]

Therefore a sufficient practical same-shell criterion is
\[
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

So the same-shell benchmark-side frontier has now been reduced to the finite constants
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\quad
L_+,\quad
L_-,\quad
L_0,\quad
C_+,\quad
C_-,\quad
C_m.
}
\]

\section{Full Explicit Gate-1 Inequality for the Canonical Pure-Even Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

We now stop treating the same-shell benchmark and the residual remote budget separately.
For the explicit working branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
\]
the benchmark side and the residual side can be assembled into one finite practical Gate-1 inequality.

\section{1. Master Gate-1 structure}

The remote-gap support theorem has the fixed form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_master}
\end{equation}

The benchmark side is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:G1_bench}
\end{equation}

This is already structurally closed and reduced to finite explicit verification. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3} :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{2. Residual remote decomposition}

Write
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\]
and decompose the residual remainder as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_R(p)=R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p).
}
\label{eq:G1_R_decomp}
\end{equation}

At the minimal sectorwise level one may define pairwise budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|,
\]
so that the crude but rigorous block-norm estimate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}\le \sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_blocknorm}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, a sharper Gershgorin route is available:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_m
\Bigl(
|(H_R)_{mm}(p)|-\sum_{n\neq m}|(H_R)_{mn}(p)|
\Bigr)>0
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:G1_Gersh}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Dominant-pair reduction}

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the high--non pair is already reduced to an explicit \(O(\rho)\) remainder:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}\le C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho.
}
\label{eq:G1_highnon}
\end{equation}

Therefore the leading residual pair is the non--wrong sector, and the reduced Step-IV gate becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\,\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+
2\,C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_dominant_pair}
\end{equation}

This is the sharpened practical residual route. 

\section{4. Fully inserted residual budget}

The tail theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\label{eq:G1_tail}
\end{equation}

The diagonal correction budget is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{diag\ corr}}(p)\|.
}
\label{eq:G1_diag}
\end{equation}

The explicit non--wrong estimate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right).
}
\label{eq:G1_nonwrong}
\end{equation}

Hence the fully inserted residual budget is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_full_residual}
\end{equation}

This is the final residual-side insertion. 

\section{5. Same-shell benchmark insertion from the explicit branch}

For the explicit same-shell branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,

the same-shell usable benchmark slot was reduced to
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.

\section{Attachment of Gate 4 to the Integrated Carrier Theorem in the Actual Canonical Basis}

\section{Short explanation}

The carrier-side part is already reduced to the practical Gate-2 and Gate-3 tests.
The remaining logically independent issue is mass protection.

In the actual canonical shell basis, this is no longer a PDE problem.
It is a finite constant-operator audit on the corrected isolated doubled shell block.

\section{1. Fixed actual canonical Dirac block}

The actual projected shell block is already brought to the canonical massless form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_Hcore}
\end{equation}

Its exact residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_Qstar}
\end{equation}

The transported actual constant mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{M_1,M_2\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_Mactual}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact \(Q_*\)-commutant and exclusion of masses}

Let \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\) denote the Hermitian commutant of \(Q_*\):
\[
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):[Q_*,K]=0\}.
\]

In the actual basis one may verify directly that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_CQ}
\end{equation}

By direct comparison with \eqref{eq:G4attach_Mactual},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_intersection}
\end{equation}

Therefore every exact constant operator commuting with \(Q_*\) is automatically mass-protecting.

\section{3. Corrected constant sector}

Write the full corrected constant sector as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0).
}
\label{eq:G4attach_dHconst}
\end{equation}

The exact sufficient Gate-4 criterion is the triple commutator test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_triple}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:G4attach_triple} holds, then each source lies in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\), hence
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:G4attach_intersection},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_nomass}
\end{equation}
So Gate 4 passes.

\section{4. What is already closed for the current branch}

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the shell-block-level Class II correction remains purely derivative and preserves the valley generator.
Therefore no independent constant shell mass is inserted by the minimal corrected Class II block.

So, at shell-block level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0
}
\label{eq:G4attach_ClassII_closed}
\end{equation}
is already the natural working conclusion.

Hence the genuinely remaining microscopic Gate-4 frontier reduces to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_remaining}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Remote-symmetry inheritance criterion}

A sufficient executable condition for the remote self-energy is the existence of a Hermitian remote-sector generator \(Q_R\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*\oplus Q_R,\ H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_fullsym}
\end{equation}

Blockwise this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_L]=0,
\qquad
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_blockwise}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:G4attach_blockwise}, the remote Schur self-energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_Sigma}
\end{equation}

Thus the remote part of Gate 4 is reduced to a finite intertwiner audit for \(Q_R\).

\section{6. Full practical acceptance theorem in the actual basis}

Combine Gate 1, Gate 2, Gate 3, and Gate 4.

Gate 1:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_G1}
\end{equation}

Gate 2:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_G2}
\end{equation}

Gate 3:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:G4attach_G3}
\end{equation}

Gate 4:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0
\Longrightarrow
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4attach_G4}
\end{equation}

Therefore the branch is practically accepted as a protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

Equivalently, in the actual basis, a sufficient practical version is

\boxed{

\begin{equation}

\label{eq:G4attach_fullaccept_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest frontier}

At this point the theorem architecture is finished.

The remaining microscopic work is not a new structural theorem.
It is the finite execution problem:
\begin{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

For the actual canonical shell basis, the corrected mass-protection problem is no longer a PDE problem.

\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,

every exact constant operator commuting with \(Q_*\) is automatically mass-protecting.

then

so Gate 4 passes.

\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},

\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad

It is no longer conceptual.

\section{Actual Low-Block Constant Audit: Direct Verification of \texorpdfstring{$[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0$}{[Q*,Hconst]=0}}

\section{Short explanation}

In the actual canonical basis, Gate 4 is no longer a classification problem.
The actual mass space is already known, and the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant is already known.
So the low-block constant audit reduces to a direct commutator computation.

The key point is that, after the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction is removed, the remaining allowed scalar constant sector is
\[
a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*.
\]
Since this commutes with \(Q_*\) identically, the low-block constant audit is closed.

\section{1. Actual canonical basis data}

The projected massless shell block in the actual canonical basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
}
\label{eq:LB_Hcore}
\end{equation}

Its exact residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:LB_Qstar}
\end{equation}

The transported actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:LB_Mactual}
\end{equation}

The exact Hermitian \(Q_*\)-commutant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_3\otimes s_3,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:LB_CQ}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:LB_intersection}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Structure of the low-block constant sector}

After the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction is removed, the remaining symmetry-preserving scalar constant sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{(\mathrm{allowed})}
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_*\,Q_*.
}
\label{eq:LB_scalar_allowed}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual low-block triplet constant sector has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_*\,Q_*.
}
\label{eq:LB_Hconst_form}
\end{equation}

This is the exact low-block content once the scalar obstruction has already been eliminated.

\section{3. Direct commutator calculation}

Now compute
\begin{align}
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]
&=
[Q_*,a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*]
\nonumber\\
&=
a_0[Q_*,\mathbf 1_4]+a_*[Q_*,Q_*]
\nonumber\\
&=
0+0.
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:LB_comm_zero}
\end{equation}

So the low-block constant sector belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commutant:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}.
}
\label{eq:LB_Hconst_in_CQ}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:LB_intersection}, it follows that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:LB_no_mass}
\end{equation}

Hence the direct low-block constant sector cannot generate an actual Dirac mass.

\section{4. Relation to the full corrected constant sector}

The full corrected constant sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}
+
\Sigma(0,0).
}
\label{eq:LB_dHconst}
\end{equation}

At shell-block level, the corrected Class II constant block is already known to be zero under natural odd shell parity, or more weakly to lie in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\setminus \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}\setminus \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}.
}
\label{eq:LB_ClassII}
\end{equation}

For the remote self-energy, if the exact same residual symmetry is preserved by remote elimination, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:LB_Sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

Therefore, once the remote inheritance audit is passed, the full corrected constant sector satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*},
}
\label{eq:LB_dH_in_CQ}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:LB_full_nomass}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Consequence for Gate 4}

The Gate-4 criterion in the actual basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:LB_G4crit}
\end{equation}

The first item is now explicitly verified by \eqref{eq:LB_comm_zero}.
So the only genuinely remaining microscopic Gate-4 frontier is the remote inheritance audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:LB_last_frontier}
\end{equation}

A constructive sufficient route is the existence of a Hermitian remote generator \(Q_R\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_R,H_R]=0,
\qquad
Q_*W=WQ_R.
}
\label{eq:LB_QRroute}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:LB_QRroute}, the Schur self-energy inherits the same \(Q_*\)-symmetry and Gate 4 fully passes.

\section{Final Summary}

In the actual canonical basis, the residual generator and actual mass space are
\[
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\qquad
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\]

The exact \(Q_*\)-commutant satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

After the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction is removed, the allowed low-block scalar constant sector is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_*\,Q_*.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]
=
[Q_*,a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*]
=0.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

So the low-block constant audit is closed.

At shell-block level, the corrected Class II constant block is already harmless:
\[
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}\setminus \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}.
}
\]

Therefore the only genuinely remaining microscopic Gate-4 frontier is the remote self-energy inheritance test
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

A constructive sufficient route is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R\ \text{Hermitian such that}\ [Q_R,H_R]=0,\quad Q_*W=WQ_R.
}
\]
Under this condition, the Schur self-energy inherits the same \(Q_*\)-symmetry and Gate 4 fully passes.

\section{Actual Remote-Sector Closure of Gate 4: Route I Closure in the Working Truncation and Route II Construction for Enlarged Truncations}

\section{Short explanation}

The remaining Gate-4 frontier was the remote-sector inheritance audit
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]
There are two exact routes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Route I: prove \(V(0)=0\) by strict shell-relevant label mismatch;
\item Route II: construct a Hermitian remote generator \(Q_R\) such that
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
\]
\end{enumerate}

In the present working truncation, Route I is already enough to close the remote-sector part of Gate 4.
Route II remains the correct extension for enlarged dangerous truncations.

\section{1. Actual shell-relevant local carrier}

The shell-relevant local carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:remote_HD}
\end{equation}

The shell-relevant mismatch labels are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\qquad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\qquad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\qquad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\qquad
\text{extra conserved microscopic labels}.
}
\label{eq:remote_labels}
\end{equation}

A remote sector is excluded from constant mixing as soon as it fails to match \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of these labels.

\section{2. Actual remote-sector decomposition}

The canonical dangerous decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
}
\label{eq:remote_HR}
\end{equation}

The first four sectors are excluded immediately:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\label{eq:remote_zero1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_zero2}
\end{equation}

So the only possible dangerous sector is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
\]

\section{3. Route I closure in the actual working truncation}

For the present working truncation we impose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing.
}
\label{eq:remote_extra_empty}
\end{equation}

Then every remote sector fails at least one shell-relevant mismatch test, hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_Hom_zero}
\end{equation}

Since the constant remote mixing block satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
}
\label{eq:remote_VHom}
\end{equation}
it follows that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_V0}
\end{equation}

This already closes the remote constant-mixing audit in the working truncation.

\section{4. Consequence for the Schur self-energy}

At constant order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:remote_sigma_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:remote_V0},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_sigma_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_sigma_comm_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence the remote-sector part of Gate 4 passes automatically in the working truncation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:remote_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Full Gate-4 consequence in the working truncation}

The low-block constant audit has already been reduced to
\[
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
\]
With \eqref{eq:remote_sigma_comm_zero}, the full corrected constant sector obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}]=0.

\label{eq:remote_total_comm}
\end{equation}

Since
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},

\label{eq:remote_CQ_mass}

one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:remote_total_nomass}
\end{equation}

So Gate 4 is closed in the working truncation.

\section{6. Route II construction for enlarged dangerous truncations}

If \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\neq \varnothing\), Route I may fail.
Then the correct constructive replacement is Route II.

The actual residual generator on the low shell block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:remote_Qstar}
\end{equation}

Choose the actual canonical shell basis
\[
|G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle,
\]
with \(s_3u_1=+u_1\), \(s_3u_2=-u_2\), and \(\tau_3|G_\pm\rangle=\pm |G_\pm\rangle\).
Then the low carrier decomposes into \(Q_*\)-charge sectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D=\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\oplus \mathcal H_D^{(-)},
}
\label{eq:remote_HDcharge}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D^{(+)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle\},
\qquad
\mathcal H_D^{(-)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle\}.
}
\label{eq:remote_HDpm}
\end{equation}

Now decompose the remote sector into charge sectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_{q\in\mathcal Q}\mathcal H_R^{(q)},
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(q)}}=q\,\mathbf 1.
}
\label{eq:remote_QR_decomp}
\end{equation}

The intertwiner condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R
}
\label{eq:remote_intertwiner}
\end{equation}
is equivalent to the selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_D^{(q)}
\quad\text{only.}
}
\label{eq:remote_selection}
\end{equation}

So the finite Route-II audit is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item decompose \(\mathcal H_R\) into exact residual sectors;
\item assign each dangerous remote sector a \(Q_R\)-charge \(q=\pm1\);
\item check whether every nonzero block of \(V(0)\) preserves the charge;
\item verify
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

If these hold, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:remote_routeII_sigma}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Two-route closure theorem in actual form}

Therefore the remote sector passes Gate 4 if either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:remote_routeI}

or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\quad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.

\label{eq:remote_routeII}
\end{equation}

In the present working truncation, Route I already holds by \eqref{eq:remote_extra_empty}, so Route II is not needed for closure at this level.

\section{8. Full practical accept condition now simplifies}

Combining Gate 1, Gate 2, Gate 3, and the working-truncation Route-I Gate-4 closure, the explicit practical accept condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

\label{eq:remote_full_accept}
\end{equation}

But in the working truncation,
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Sigma(0,0)=0,
\]
so the only remaining constant-sector check is the already-completed low-block one. Therefore the practical branch is fully accepted once the carrier and support gates pass.

\section{9. Honest status}

At this point the theorem architecture is finished.

For the working truncation, Gate 4 is closed by Route I.
For enlarged dangerous truncations, the remaining work is the finite Route-II charge-sector audit:
\[
Q_R,\qquad [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\qquad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
\]

So the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is only the finite sectorwise content of \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\), if one chooses to enlarge beyond the current working truncation.

\section{Final Summary}

For the actual remote-sector Gate-4 audit, there are two exact routes.

\paragraph{Route I: strict shell-relevant mismatch.}
If
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger=0,
}
\]
so the remote sector automatically passes Gate 4.

In the present working truncation,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing,
}
\]
and each displayed sector fails at least one shell-relevant mismatch label relative to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
}
\]

So, in the present working truncation, the remote-sector part of Gate 4 is already closed by Route I.

\paragraph{Route II: exact residual intertwiner symmetry.}
If the truncation is enlarged and \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\neq\varnothing\), the constructive sufficient route is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\qquad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
}
\]
In the actual canonical basis,
\[
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\]
and the low shell carrier decomposes into charges
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D^{(+)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle\},
\qquad
\mathcal H_D^{(-)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle\}.
}
\]
Then the finite audit is to decompose
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_{q}\mathcal H_R^{(q)},
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(q)}}=q\,\mathbf 1,
\]
and verify the charge-selection rule
\[
\boxed{
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\to \mathcal H_D^{(q)}\quad\text{only.}
}
\]
If this holds, then
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Bottom line.}
For the current working truncation, Route I already gives
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0,\qquad \Sigma(0,0)=0,
}
\]
so Gate 4 is closed once the low-block constant audit is combined with this result.

Therefore the practical full-branch acceptance condition is now
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]
In the working truncation, the remote part contributes no constant mass because

\]

\section{Actual Route-II Charge-Table Construction for Enlarged Dangerous Truncations}

\section{Short explanation}

In the working truncation, Route I already closes the remote-sector part of Gate 4 because
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
\]
So Route II is only needed when the truncation is enlarged and an actually dangerous extra sector appears.

We now write the concrete \(Q_R\)-construction in the actual canonical basis.

\section{1. Low-shell charge decomposition}

The actual low-shell residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:RII_Qstar}
\end{equation}

Fix the actual canonical shell basis
\[
|G_+,u_1\rangle,\quad |G_+,u_2\rangle,\quad |G_-,u_1\rangle,\quad |G_-,u_2\rangle,
\]
with
\[
\tau_3|G_\pm\rangle=\pm |G_\pm\rangle,
\qquad
s_3u_1=+u_1,
\qquad
s_3u_2=-u_2.
\]
Then the four low-shell states carry charges
\[
q(G_+,u_1)=+1,\qquad
q(G_+,u_2)=-1,\qquad
q(G_-,u_1)=-1,\qquad
q(G_-,u_2)=+1.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D^{(+)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle\},
\qquad
\mathcal H_D^{(-)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle\}.
}
\label{eq:RII_HDpm}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Which remote states can be dangerous}

A remote state can be dangerous for constant mixing only if it matches the shell-relevant labels of \(\mathcal H_D\):
\[
\pm G_*,
\qquad
\text{non-volumetric character},
\qquad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\qquad
\text{compatible grading/parity},
\]
up to additional microscopic labels that do not forbid intertwining.

Therefore the enlarged dangerous sector is the direct sum
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:RII_Hextra}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(+)}\): remote states that can mix only with \(\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\);
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(-)}\): remote states that can mix only with \(\mathcal H_D^{(-)}\);
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}\): remote states that still fail at least one decisive label and therefore must not mix at constant order.
\end{itemize}

\section{3. Definition of the remote generator \(Q_R\)}

Define \(Q_R\) by charge assignment
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(+)}}=+\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(-)}}=-\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}}=0.
}
\label{eq:RII_QR_def}
\end{equation}

If the rest of the remote sector still belongs to the strict mismatch part
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
we also assign charge \(0\) there:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{safe\ mismatch}}}=0.
}
\label{eq:RII_QR_safe}
\end{equation}

So the full remote space decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_R^{(+)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_R^{(-)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_R^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:RII_HR_charge}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal H_R^{(+)}:=\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(+)},
\qquad
\mathcal H_R^{(-)}:=\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(-)},
\]
and
\[
\mathcal H_R^{(0)}
:=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{safe\ mismatch}}.
\]

\section{4. Intertwiner condition as an explicit block table}

Write the constant remote mixing block in charge components:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
V_{++} & V_{+-} & V_{+0}\\
V_{-+} & V_{--} & V_{-0}
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:RII_Vblocks}
\end{equation}
where columns are ordered by
\[
\mathcal H_R^{(+)}\oplus \mathcal H_R^{(-)}\oplus \mathcal H_R^{(0)},
\]
and rows by
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\oplus \mathcal H_D^{(-)}.
\]

Then the exact intertwiner condition
\[
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R
\]
is equivalent to the blockwise selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{+-}=0,\qquad
V_{-+}=0,\qquad
V_{+0}=0,\qquad
V_{-0}=0,
}
\label{eq:RII_selection_zero}
\end{equation}
while \(V_{++}\) and \(V_{--}\) are allowed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{++}\ \text{arbitrary},
\qquad
V_{--}\ \text{arbitrary}.
}
\label{eq:RII_selection_allowed}
\end{equation}

So the actual finite Route-II audit is literally:
\[
\boxed{
\text{only charge-preserving remote-to-low blocks may be nonzero.}
}
\]

\section{5. Commutation with the remote block}

To complete Route II, one also needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:RII_HR_comm}
\end{equation}

In the charge basis \(\mathcal H_R^{(+)}\oplus\mathcal H_R^{(-)}\oplus\mathcal H_R^{(0)}\), this means
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_R(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{R,+} & 0 & 0\\
0 & H_{R,-} & 0\\
0 & 0 & H_{R,0}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:RII_HR_blockdiag}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the off-charge remote blocks must vanish:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(H_R)_{+-}=(H_R)_{-+}=(H_R)_{+0}=(H_R)_{0+}=(H_R)_{-0}=(H_R)_{0-}=0.
}
\label{eq:RII_HR_offdiag_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus the Route-II audit is finite on two levels:
\begin{enumerate}
\item charge-preserving structure of \(V(0)\);
\item charge-block-diagonal structure of \(H_R(0)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Charge-table summary}

The complete actual charge table is:

\begin{center}
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{sector} & \text{basis content} & Q\text{-charge} \\ \hline
\mathcal H_D^{(+)} & |G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle & +1 \\
\mathcal H_D^{(-)} & |G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle & -1 \\ \hline
\mathcal H_R^{(+)} & \text{dangerous extra states matching } \mathcal H_D^{(+)} & +1 \\
\mathcal H_R^{(-)} & \text{dangerous extra states matching } \mathcal H_D^{(-)} & -1 \\
\mathcal H_R^{(0)} & \text{strict mismatch remote states} & 0
\end{array}
\]
\end{center}

Under this table, the exact Route-II selection rule is simply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{constant mixing preserves charge } q\in\{+1,-1\},
\quad
q=0\text{ never mixes into } \mathcal H_D.
}
\label{eq:RII_charge_table_rule}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Consequence for the self-energy}

Since
\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\]
the inverse resolvent also commutes with \(Q_R\). Therefore
\begin{align}
Q_*\Sigma(0,0)
&=
Q_*V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger \\
&=
V(0)Q_R\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger \\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}Q_RV(0)^\dagger \\
&=
V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger Q_* \\
&=
\Sigma(0,0)Q_*.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:RII_sigma_comm_final}
\end{equation}

Because every actual mass generator fails to commute with \(Q_*\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:RII_sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Final practical Gate-4 statement}

Therefore:
\begin{itemize}
\item in the current working truncation, Route I already gives
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Sigma(0,0)=0;
\]
\item in enlarged dangerous truncations, Route II is reduced to the finite charge-table audit
\[
Q_R,\qquad [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\qquad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
\]
\end{itemize}

So Gate 4 is fully finite and executable in both cases.

\section{Final Summary}

For the remote-sector part of Gate 4 there are two exact routes.

\paragraph{Route I.}
If
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
\]
In the current working truncation,
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing,
\]
so this route already closes the remote-sector part of Gate 4.

\paragraph{Route II.}
For enlarged dangerous truncations, decompose the low carrier as
\[
\mathcal H_D=\mathcal H_D^{(+)}\oplus\mathcal H_D^{(-)},
\]
with
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(+)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_1\rangle,\ |G_-,u_2\rangle\},
\qquad
\mathcal H_D^{(-)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|G_+,u_2\rangle,\ |G_-,u_1\rangle\},
\]
under
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
\]

Then decompose the dangerous remote sector into
\[
\mathcal H_R=\mathcal H_R^{(+)}\oplus\mathcal H_R^{(-)}\oplus\mathcal H_R^{(0)},
\]
and define
\[
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(+)}}=+1,\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(-)}}=-1,\qquad
Q_R|_{\mathcal H_R^{(0)}}=0.
\]

The finite Route-II audit is:

\[
[Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,
\qquad
Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
\]

In block form, this is equivalent to:

\[
V(0):\mathcal H_R^{(q)}\to\mathcal H_D^{(q)}
\quad\text{only},
\]
and
\[
H_R(0)\ \text{is block diagonal in the charge sectors }q=+1,-1,0.
\]

If these hold, then
\[
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\]
hence
\[
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{in the working truncation, Gate 4 is already closed by Route I;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{in enlarged dangerous truncations, Gate 4 reduces to a finite Route-II charge-table audit.}
}
\]

\section{Practical Full-Branch Acceptance Theorem in the Working Truncation}

\section{Statement of the branch}

We fix the explicit canonical branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\eta=z_0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\label{eq:PT_branch}
\end{equation}
together with the canonical carrier normalization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\label{eq:PT_norm}
\end{equation}

This is the pure-even working branch obtained after the graded \(2+2\) bypass and the explicit shell/Class-II reduction.

\section{1. Explicit carrier coefficients}

In this branch the reduced transport coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:PT_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:PT_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Hence the anisotropic Dirac determinant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:PT_det}
\end{equation}

Therefore the carrier-side nondegeneracy condition reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:PT_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Gate 1 benchmark side}

The full benchmark side is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\},
}
\label{eq:PT_bench}
\end{equation}
where the same-shell non-enriched slot is bounded below by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:PT_Xinon}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_K
=
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\label{eq:PT_aK}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 1 reduces to the explicit scalar inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:PT_G1}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Gate 1 residual side}

The fully inserted residual budget is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:PT_residual}
\end{equation}

In the present pure-even branch one may sharpen
\[
|C_E|+|C_O|\longrightarrow |C_E|=1,
\]
so the working branch residual estimate becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:PT_residual_even}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Gate 4 in the actual canonical basis}

The exact residual generator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:PT_Qstar}
\end{equation}

The actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_2\otimes\mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_1\otimes s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:PT_Mactual}
\end{equation}

After the scalar obstruction is removed, the allowed low-block constant sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}
=
a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*,
}
\label{eq:PT_Hconst}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:PT_Hconst_comm}
\end{equation}

At shell-block level, the corrected Class-II constant sector is harmless:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*}\setminus\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}.
}
\label{eq:PT_ClassII_const}
\end{equation}

For the remote sector, in the present working truncation one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:PT_RouteI}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)=V(0)\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)^\dagger=0,
}
\label{eq:PT_sigma_zero}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:PT_sigma_comm}
\end{equation}

So the full corrected constant sector obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:PT_total_const_comm}
\end{equation}

Since the exact \(Q_*\)-commutant satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:PT_CQ_intersection}
\end{equation}
it follows that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:PT_no_mass}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 4 is closed in the working truncation.

\section{5. Practical full-branch acceptance theorem}

Combining Gate 1, Gate 2, Gate 3, and Gate 4, we obtain the following.

\paragraph{Practical Full-Branch Acceptance Theorem.}
Assume the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
\]
and suppose:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\label{eq:PT_assume1}
\end{equation}
with \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}\) and \(\eta_{R,\rho}\) given by
\eqref{eq:PT_bench} and \eqref{eq:PT_residual_even};

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,\qquad \beta_X\neq0,\qquad \theta_0\kappa\neq0;
}
\label{eq:PT_assume2}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\quad\text{(working truncation Route I)}.
}
\label{eq:PT_assume3}
\end{equation}

Then:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:PT_conclusion}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the branch is accepted as a protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch.

\section{6. Proof}

From \eqref{eq:PT_assume1} and the remote-gap support theorem, one gets
\[
\Delta_\rho>0.
\]

From \eqref{eq:PT_lambda} and \eqref{eq:PT_assume2},
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq0.
\]

From \eqref{eq:PT_alpha_beta} and \eqref{eq:PT_assume2},
\[
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa
\neq0,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
hence
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
\]

Finally, \eqref{eq:PT_Hconst_comm}, \eqref{eq:PT_ClassII_const}, and \eqref{eq:PT_sigma_comm} imply
\[
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}]=0.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:PT_CQ_intersection},
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\},
\]
so
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:PT_conclusion}.
\qed

\section{7. Honest frontier beyond the working truncation}

The theorem above is practical and fully executable in the present working truncation.

The only stronger frontier is the enlarged dangerous truncation, where one allows
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\neq\varnothing.
\]
In that case the remaining sufficient route is the finite charge-table audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\qquad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
}
\label{eq:PT_QR}
\end{equation}

This is not needed for closure at the current working-theorem level, but it is the correct stronger extension.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical working branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
the carrier coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\]

The full benchmark side is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\},
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\]

The working-branch residual side is bounded by
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

In the working truncation, Route I gives
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\Sigma(0,0)=0.
}
\]
Together with
\[
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}=a_0\mathbf 1_4+a_*Q_*,
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
}
\]
this implies
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore, if
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}^{(\mathrm{full})}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\]

Hence the branch is practically accepted as a protected anisotropic massless Dirac branch in the current working truncation.

The only stronger frontier beyond this theorem is the enlarged dangerous truncation, where one would need the finite Route-II audit
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,Q_R:\ [Q_R,H_R(0)]=0,\qquad Q_*V(0)=V(0)Q_R.
}
\]

\section{Completed Working-Branch Infrared PDE}

\section{Working-branch statement}

We fix the explicit canonical working branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\eta=z_0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
together with the canonical carrier normalization
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\]

At the practical theorem level, this branch is accepted when
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the branch realizes a spectrally isolated, mass-protected anisotropic massless Dirac block
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\]

\section{Exact Branch-B coefficient dictionary}

In Branch B the coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:completed_dict}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit defect overlaps
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:completed_lambda_general}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:completed_alpha_beta_general}
\end{equation}

\section{Pure-even explicit working realization}

In the current explicit pure-even Class-II working realization one may identify
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:completed_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:completed_alpha_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

Thus the determinant of the reduced transport matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:completed_det}
\end{equation}

Therefore the carrier-side nondegeneracy condition reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:completed_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Completed infrared PDE}

The completed working-branch infrared equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
\beta\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:completed_IR_PDE}
\end{equation}

In the explicit pure-even realization \(\beta=0\), so this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:completed_IR_PDE_even}
\end{equation}
with \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha\) given by \eqref{eq:completed_lambda_explicit} and \eqref{eq:completed_alpha_beta_explicit}.

\section{Equivalent principal symbol}

Equivalently, the principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:completed_symbol}
\end{equation}

For the pure-even working branch this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:completed_symbol_even}
\end{equation}

\section{What is completed versus what is not}

What is completed at the practical working-branch level is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact PDE form \eqref{eq:completed_IR_PDE};
\item the Branch-B coefficient dictionary \eqref{eq:completed_dict};
\item the explicit pure-even working coefficients \eqref{eq:completed_lambda_explicit}--\eqref{eq:completed_alpha_beta_explicit};
\item the practical acceptance criterion
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet closed as a fully unconditional final microscopic theorem is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the final explicit overlap insertions \(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O\) in the most general microscopic realization;
\item the final corrected residual-symmetry audit after remote-sector elimination in arbitrary enlarged dangerous truncations;
\item the compatible parameter region where all practical gates hold simultaneously.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct final wording is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the infrared PDE is completed at practical working-branch level,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{full unconditional microscopic completion still depends on the remaining finite audits.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Completed Coefficient Sheet for the Current Working Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

The only honest remaining issue is not the PDE form, but the final insertion of the branch-specific microscopic calibration constants.

\section{1. Exact overlap dictionary}

\qquad

=

\end{equation}

\section{2. Longitudinal column: two equivalent working parameterizations}

The uploaded notes currently contain two branch-level longitudinal parameterizations.

\subsection{2.1 One-mediator shell-projected form}

The one-mediator shell-projected Branch-B formula is

\section{Final Coefficient Sheet with Explicit Bloch Calibration Layer}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the reduced infrared PDE form is already fixed.
The remaining coefficient-finding problem is no longer the derivation of the PDE structure itself.
It is the explicit separation of:

\[
\text{transport-side coefficient point }(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\]
from
\[
\text{Bloch overlap calibration } \mathbb C.
\]

The exact physical coefficients are obtained only after the final shell-projected Bloch calibration.

\section{1. Exact transport/Bloch dictionary}

The exact normalization layer is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\
\alpha\\
\beta
\end{pmatrix}
=
\mathbb C
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\
g_E\\
g_O
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_matrix_dict}
\end{equation}

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact, the calibration matrix is diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O),
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_diagC}
\end{equation}
and then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_diag_dict}
\end{equation}

In the more general mildly mixed case, one must use the full matrix criterion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_mixed_criterion}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Current branch-level transport coefficient point}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side point is already explicit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_gpoint}
\end{equation}

Thus, after diagonal calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
j^2,
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_lambda_after_cal}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,

\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,
I_\theta\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:finalsheet_alpha_beta_after_cal}
\end{equation}

The explicit defect overlaps are

\section{3. Longitudinal calibration constant as a direct shell matrix-element audit}

The final longitudinal coefficient is read from the projected shell-normal matrix

Equivalently, in the \(+\)-valley \(2\times2\) internal block,

Comparing \eqref{eq:finalsheet_lambda_trace} with the one-mediator shell normalization,

Therefore the remaining longitudinal coefficient audit is no longer broad or conceptual.

\boxed{
M_{11}-M_{22}\neq 0.

\label{eq:finalsheet_last_long_test}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Why \(C_\parallel=0\) is not symmetry-protected}

At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the primitive longitudinal channel is the unique singlet-to-singlet intertwiner
\[

Therefore vanishing of \(C_\parallel\) is not enforced by the minimal shell symmetry.

Moreover, if the carrier doublet \(u_1,u_2\) is actually split by an exact grading/parity/chirality label \(J\), or differs by any additional exact conserved microscopic label, then no label-preserving exchange involution can force
\[

Hence
\begin{equation}

C_\parallel=0

\section{5. Transverse calibration layer}

\end{equation}
or, in the mixed case, the rank condition \eqref{eq:finalsheet_mixed_criterion}.

but

\boxed{

}

\section{Final Summary}

The exact reduced infrared coefficients are obtained from the transport-side point
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O)

only after the final Bloch calibration:

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side coefficient point is already explicit:
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},

It is the finite Bloch calibration audit of
