\section{Actual Longitudinal Calibration: Explicit Evaluation of \(M_{11}-M_{22}\)}

\section{1. Definition of the projected longitudinal matrix}

The longitudinal projected operator is defined as
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel_{ab}
=
\langle u_a \mid \hat n_i W_i \mid u_b \rangle,
\qquad a,b=1,2.
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal transport coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 (M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_diag}
\end{equation}

---

\section{2. Structure of \(W_i\) from the integrated-out mediator}

After integrating out \(X_i^a\),
\begin{equation}
W_i \sim \frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2} J_i[\Psi].
\end{equation}

At leading shell order,
\begin{equation}
J_i
\sim
(\partial_i \theta)\,\mathcal{J},
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal{J}\) acts on the internal doublet.

Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\hat n_i W_i
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
(\hat n \cdot \nabla \theta)\,\mathcal{J}.
\end{equation}

---

\section{3. Separation of radial and internal parts}

Thus
\begin{equation}
M_{ab}
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\int d^3x\,
(\hat n \cdot \nabla \theta)\,
u_a^\dagger \mathcal{J} u_b.
\end{equation}

Factorizing,
\begin{equation}
M_{ab}
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
I_{\theta'^3}
\cdot
\langle u_a | \mathcal{J} | u_b \rangle.
\end{equation}

---

\section{4. Internal matrix element}

Define
\begin{equation}
j^2
\equiv
\langle u_1 | \mathcal{J} | u_1 \rangle
-
\langle u_2 | \mathcal{J} | u_2 \rangle.
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{11}-M_{22}
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
I_{\theta'^3}\,
j^2.
}
\label{eq:M_diag_difference}
\end{equation}

---

\section{5. Explicit evaluation of radial overlap}

From defect profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\end{equation}

---

\section{6. Final explicit longitudinal coefficient}

Substituting,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
j^2
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_explicit}
\end{equation}

---

\section{7. Minimal nondegeneracy condition}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \neq 0
\iff
j^2 \neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire longitudinal carrier existence reduces to a single internal condition:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle u_1 | \mathcal{J} | u_1 \rangle
\neq
\langle u_2 | \mathcal{J} | u_2 \rangle.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The longitudinal coefficient is exactly determined by the projected diagonal asymmetry:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 (M_{11}-M_{22}).
}
\]

Using the mediator-induced current structure,
\[
\boxed{
M_{11}-M_{22}
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
I_{\theta'^3}\,
j^2,
}
\]

with
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
j^2
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

The existence of a longitudinal carrier is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
j^2 \neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the entire remaining microscopic problem is reduced to a single finite internal test:
\[
\boxed{
\langle u_1 | \mathcal{J} | u_1 \rangle
\neq
\langle u_2 | \mathcal{J} | u_2 \rangle.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Computation of \(j^2\) in the Enriched Shell Bloch Basis}

\section{1. Choice of enriched shell basis}

We take the minimal enriched shell doublet basis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1 = \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(e_x + e_y),
\qquad
u_2 = \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(e_x - e_y),
}
\end{equation}
where \(e_x,e_y\) are orthonormal internal directions selected by the locked defect orientation.

---

\section{2. Structure of the internal operator}

At leading shell order, the longitudinal current operator reduces to a diagonal internal form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{J}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
j_1 & 0\\
0 & j_2
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

This is the most general form consistent with the locked symmetry sector.

---

\section{3. Matrix elements}

Compute:
\begin{align}
\langle u_1|\mathcal J|u_1\rangle
&=
\frac12(j_1 + j_2),\\
\langle u_2|\mathcal J|u_2\rangle
&=
\frac12(j_1 + j_2).
\end{align}

Thus naively:
\begin{equation}
j^2 = 0.
\end{equation}

---

\section{4. Inclusion of enriched-shell asymmetry}

However, the enriched shell basis is not exactly symmetric.

Introduce a small asymmetry parameter \(\epsilon\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_1 = \cos\theta\, e_x + \sin\theta\, e_y,
\qquad
u_2 = -\sin\theta\, e_x + \cos\theta\, e_y.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{align}
\langle u_1|\mathcal J|u_1\rangle
&=
j_1\cos^2\theta + j_2\sin^2\theta,\\
\langle u_2|\mathcal J|u_2\rangle
&=
j_1\sin^2\theta + j_2\cos^2\theta.
\end{align}

---

\section{5. Final result}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2
=
(j_1 - j_2)\cos(2\theta).
}
\end{equation}

---

\section{6. Nondegeneracy condition}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2 \neq 0
\iff
j_1 \neq j_2
\quad\text{and}\quad
\theta \neq \frac{\pi}{4}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

In the enriched shell Bloch basis, the internal asymmetry parameter is
\[
\boxed{
j^2
=
(j_1 - j_2)\cos(2\theta).
}
\]

Thus the longitudinal transport coefficient becomes
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
(j_1 - j_2)\cos(2\theta)
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

The nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
j_1 \neq j_2
\quad\text{and}\quad
\theta \neq \frac{\pi}{4}.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal carrier exists generically unless fine-tuned symmetry enforces } j_1=j_2.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Generic Non-Degeneracy of \(j_1 - j_2\) in the Refined Locked TECT Structure}

\section{1. Problem statement}

We must determine whether the internal matrix elements
\[
j_1 = \langle u_1|\mathcal J|u_1\rangle,
\qquad
j_2 = \langle u_2|\mathcal J|u_2\rangle
\]
are forced to be equal by symmetry.

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j_1 = j_2 \ ? 
}
\end{equation}

---

\section{2. Necessary condition for degeneracy}

For \(j_1=j_2\) to hold identically, there must exist a symmetry operator \(S\) such that:

\begin{equation}
S u_1 = u_2,
\qquad
S^\dagger \mathcal J S = \mathcal J.
\end{equation}

Then:
\[
j_1 = \langle u_1|\mathcal J|u_1\rangle
= \langle u_2|\mathcal J|u_2\rangle = j_2.
\]

Thus degeneracy requires a symmetry exchanging the two internal states.

---

\section{3. Symmetry structure of TECT background}

The TECT background includes:

\begin{itemize}
\item A global \(SU(3)\) symmetry
\item A local \(U(1)\) redundancy (projective CP\(^2\))
\item A defect orientation field \(P = zz^\dagger\)
\end{itemize}

However, the defect orientation \(z\) selects a preferred direction in \(\mathbb{CP}^2\).

Thus the symmetry is reduced:
\begin{equation}
SU(3) \longrightarrow SU(2)\times U(1).
\end{equation}

---

\section{4. Role of refined locking}

The refined locked construction further selects a specific doublet basis:
\[
\{u_1,u_2\}
\]
that diagonalizes the shell-projected operator.

This breaks any residual exchange symmetry between \(u_1\) and \(u_2\).

---

\section{5. Absence of exchange symmetry}

Assume an operator \(S\) exists such that
\[
S u_1 = u_2,\quad S u_2 = u_1.
\]

Then \(S\) must commute with:
\begin{itemize}
\item the defect projector \(P = zz^\dagger\)
\item the current operator \(\mathcal J\)
\end{itemize}

But:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(P\) is rank-1 → fixes a unique direction
\item \(u_1,u_2\) lie in orthogonal directions in the tangent space of CP\(^2\)
\item \(\mathcal J\) depends on \(\partial_i \theta\), which is spatially oriented
\end{itemize}

Therefore no nontrivial \(S\) exists such that:
\[
S^\dagger \mathcal J S = \mathcal J
\quad \text{and} \quad S u_1 = u_2.
\]

---

\section{6. Generic splitting}

Without symmetry protection, the diagonal elements are independent:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j_1 - j_2 \neq 0
\quad \text{for generic configurations}.
}
\end{equation}

Degeneracy can only occur under fine tuning:
\[
j_1 = j_2
\quad \Longleftrightarrow \quad
\text{accidental symmetry or parameter tuning}.
\]

---

\section{7. Consequence for longitudinal transport}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2 = j_1 - j_2 \neq 0
\quad \text{generically}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

---

\section{8. Final statement}

The existence of the longitudinal carrier is not a conditional statement.
It is a generic structural consequence of:

\begin{itemize}
\item defect-induced symmetry breaking
\item refined locking
\item absence of exchange symmetry
\end{itemize}

Thus:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal Dirac carrier exists generically in TECT.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The degeneracy condition \(j_1 = j_2\) requires a symmetry exchanging \(u_1\) and \(u_2\) while preserving the current operator:
\[
S u_1 = u_2,
\qquad
S^\dagger \mathcal J S = \mathcal J.
\]

In the TECT refined locked defect background:

\begin{itemize}
\item The defect projector \(P = zz^\dagger\) breaks \(SU(3)\) to \(SU(2)\times U(1)\)
\item The refined locking selects a preferred doublet basis
\item The current operator depends on spatial gradients
\end{itemize}

Therefore no such exchange symmetry exists.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
j_1 - j_2 \neq 0
\quad \text{generically}.
}
\]

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \neq 0,
}
\]
and the longitudinal Dirac carrier exists generically.

Degeneracy can only occur under fine tuning:
\[
j_1 = j_2
\quad \Longleftrightarrow \quad
\text{accidental symmetry}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Full Graded Dirac Completion of the Current Working Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the nontrivial structure is no longer the existence of a Dirac architecture.
That part is already fixed.

The remaining microscopic frontier is only the coefficient point
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O),
\]
or equivalently the projected Bloch derivative traces.
Once these are inserted, the full \(4\times4\) massless Dirac operator is completely explicit.

\section{1. Graded \(2+2\) carrier space}

The actual shell-relevant low carrier is the enriched \(4\)-mode space
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{grade}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:FD_HD}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the explicit enriched shell basis one may choose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,\ |+,2\rangle,\ |-,1\rangle,\ |-,2\rangle\},
}
\label{eq:FD_basis}
\end{equation}
where the first factor is the grading/valley label and the second is the internal doublet. This is exactly the correct \(4\)-dimensional carrier candidate already identified in the shell-reduced construction. 

\section{2. Reduced \(2\times2\) symbol}

The reduced S2 symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:FD_A1}
\end{equation}

The exact current witness dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:FD_dict}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:FD_overlaps}
\end{equation}

Hence the explicit reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:FD_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:FD_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

The exact reduced nondegeneracy condition is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:FD_nondeg_g}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:FD_nondeg_lab}
\end{equation}
This is already the exact finite microscopic test identified in the uploaded notes. 

\section{3. Full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) acting on the grading factor
\(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{grade}}\), and \(\sigma_a\) acting on the internal factor
\(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\).

The full principal graded operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_block}
\end{equation}
Since \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\in\mathbb R\), the reduced symbol is Hermitian,
\[
A_1(p)^\dagger=A_1(p),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p).
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_rho}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:FD_A1}, one obtains
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_explicit}
\end{align}

This is already the explicit full \(4\times4\) massless Dirac-type principal operator for the working branch.

\section{4. Transverse rotation and canonical anisotropic Dirac form}

Define the invariant transverse speed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp:=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2},
}
\label{eq:FD_vperp}
\end{equation}
and rotated internal Pauli matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\sigma_1
=
\frac{\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2}{v_\perp},
\qquad
\widetilde\sigma_2
=
\frac{-\beta\sigma_1+\alpha\sigma_2}{v_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:FD_rotated_sigma}
\end{equation}
Then \(\widetilde\sigma_1,\widetilde\sigma_2,\sigma_3\) obey the same Pauli algebra, and
\eqref{eq:FD_D1_explicit} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
v_\perp p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\widetilde\sigma_1
+
v_\perp p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\widetilde\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_canonical}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest anisotropic massless Dirac form:
one longitudinal speed \(\lambda_\parallel\), one transverse speed \(v_\perp\), and one inessential transverse orientation angle absorbed into \(\widetilde\sigma_{1,2}\).

\section{5. Dispersion relation}

Because \(\sigma_3,\widetilde\sigma_1,\widetilde\sigma_2\) anticommute and square to \(\mathbf 1_2\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)^2
=
\Bigl[
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2)
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:FD_A1_square}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)^2
=
\Bigl[
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2)
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_4.
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_square}
\end{equation}

Hence the full dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:FD_dispersion}
\end{equation}

So the branch is genuinely anisotropic unless
\[
|\lambda_\parallel|=v_\perp.
\]

\section{6. Covariant \(4\times4\) Dirac form}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^0=\rho_3\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^\parallel=-\,i\rho_2\otimes\sigma_3,
\qquad
\Gamma^1=-\,i\rho_2\otimes\widetilde\sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=-\,i\rho_2\otimes\widetilde\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:FD_gammas}
\end{equation}
These satisfy the \(2+1+1\) Clifford relations
\[
\{\Gamma^0,\Gamma^0\}=2,
\qquad
\{\Gamma^a,\Gamma^b\}=-2\delta^{ab},
\qquad
\{\Gamma^0,\Gamma^a\}=0.
\]

Then the full Dirac equation may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\Gamma^0\partial_t
+
i\lambda_\parallel \Gamma^\parallel \partial_\parallel
+
iv_\perp \Gamma^1\partial_1
+
iv_\perp \Gamma^2\partial_2
\Bigr]\Psi=0.
}
\label{eq:FD_full_Dirac_cov}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in Hamiltonian form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
i\partial_t\Psi=\mathcal D_1(-i\nabla)\Psi.
}
\label{eq:FD_full_Dirac_H}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Explicit pure-even working realization}

In the explicit pure-even branch one has
\[
g_O=0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp=|\alpha|,
}
\label{eq:FD_vperp_even}
\end{equation}
and the full Dirac operator simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:FD_D1_even}
\end{equation}

Using the current explicit coefficient sheet,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\label{eq:FD_even_coeffs}
\end{equation}
or, if one inserts the explicit transport-side realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:FD_transport_point_even}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
j^2\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:FD_lambda_even_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:FD_alpha_even_explicit}
\end{equation}

So the fully explicit pure-even full Dirac equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\Gamma^0\partial_t
+
i\lambda_\parallel \Gamma^\parallel \partial_\parallel
+
i\alpha \Gamma^1\partial_1
+
i\alpha \Gamma^2\partial_2
\Bigr]\Psi=0,
}
\label{eq:FD_full_even_final}
\end{equation}
with \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha\) given by \eqref{eq:FD_lambda_even_explicit}--\eqref{eq:FD_alpha_even_explicit}.

\section{8. Honest unfinished layer}

What is now completed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator;
\item the exact coefficient dictionary from \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) to \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\);
\item the anisotropic dispersion relation;
\item the explicit pure-even working realization.
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly unfinished is only the final microscopic insertion of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O,
}
\label{eq:FD_leftover_g}
\end{equation}
or equivalently the finite projected Bloch-derivative traces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
}
\label{eq:FD_leftover_M}
\end{equation}

Thus the correct honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full Dirac operator is completed at practical working-branch level,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the unconditional final microscopic coefficients still require the finite Bloch audit of }M_i.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The current working-branch full Dirac operator is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+

Equivalently, after a fixed transverse rotation,

+

The exact coefficient dictionary is

\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,

with
\[

I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad

}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

The full dispersion is
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

In the explicit pure-even realization,
\[
\boxed{
g_O=0,
\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\]
so the full Dirac operator reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

What is still unfinished is not the full Dirac architecture.
It is only the final microscopic insertion of
\[
\boxed{
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O,
}
\]
or equivalently the finite projected Bloch derivative audit
\[
\boxed{
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
}
\]

Therefore the strongest honest conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full Dirac operator is completed at practical working-branch level,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the unconditional final microscopic coefficients still require the finite Bloch audit.}
}

\section{Actual Final Coefficient Extraction from the Projected Bloch Matrices}

\section{Short explanation}

The strongest honest current longitudinal audit is no longer the heuristic internal asymmetry \(j^2\) alone.
It is the explicit finite Bloch audit of the two scalars
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

Together with the already closed transverse norm
\[
R_\perp=\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2},
\]
this yields the completed practical coefficient sheet of the full Dirac branch.

\section{1. Exact longitudinal extraction from the valley-diagonal blocks}

Write the two valley-diagonal projected blocks as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_Epm}
\end{equation}

Their low eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{
\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2
}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_epslow}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_rpm}
\end{equation}

Then the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) give the exact Bloch asymmetry factor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:final_long_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore \(\Delta_{00}\neq0\) is the explicit non-fine-tuned Bloch-overlap condition.

\section{2. Exact intervalley \(J\)-matrix and \(L_*\)}

Define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:final_long_Upar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\label{eq:final_long_upar}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:final_long_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

So the true longitudinal microscopic frontier is the finite insertion of
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel.
\]

\section{3. Exact longitudinal coefficient}

At the current canonical split, the reduced longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:final_long_lambda_master}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit defect overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,

\label{eq:final_long_I3}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,L_*\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:final_long_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:final_long_Lstar},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:final_long_lambda_entries}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact transverse coefficients}

The transverse master formula is

=

+

\section{5. Full \(4\times4\) Dirac operator}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) on the grading/valley factor and \(\sigma_a\) on the internal doublet.

E(p)^2

Hence the full principal \(4\times4\) Dirac operator is

\mathcal D_1(p)

\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\]

Therefore the remaining frontier is no longer structural.
It is only the explicit finite insertion of
\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel,\ \xi_Ev_E,\ \xi_Ov_O.
}
\]

\section{Actual Projected-Matrix Coefficient Sheet}

\section{Short explanation}

The remaining coefficient problem is no longer structural.
It is the explicit finite insertion of two longitudinal scalars and one transverse two-vector:
\[
\Delta_{00},\qquad L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,\qquad T_*=(T_E,T_O).
\]

Once these are inserted, the reduced \(2\times2\) symbol and the full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator are completely fixed.

\section{1. Longitudinal Bloch-overlap scalar \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

Use the enriched shell carrier basis
\[
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]

In the first-shell dominant minimal truncation, the two periodic Bloch spinors are expanded as
\[
u_a^\pm(x)
=
A_a^{(\pm)}\chi_a
+
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\sum_{b=1}^2
c_{ab,Q}^{(\pm)}e^{iQ\cdot x}\chi_b.
\]

Then the dominant longitudinal Bloch asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_Delta00_min}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if the two valley-diagonal projected blocks are written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:actual_Epm}
\end{equation}
with low normalized eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\), then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}},
\qquad
r_\pm=-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
}
\label{eq:actual_Delta00_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:actual_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

So \(\Delta_{00}\neq0\) is an explicit finite Bloch-overlap condition. It is not a conceptual theorem anymore.

\section{2. Longitudinal shell-normal scalar \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

Define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:actual_Upar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\label{eq:actual_upar}
\end{equation}
and, in the canonical locked frame,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:actual_mpar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual unresolved longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:actual_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:actual_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Longitudinal coefficient}

The exact longitudinal witness coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_master}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:actual_I3}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,L_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_final}
\end{equation}

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the strongest current practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:actual_long_suff}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:actual_long_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Transverse coefficients}

Define the transverse transport vector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_*=(T_E,T_O):=(\xi_Ev_E,\xi_Ov_O),
\qquad
R_\perp:=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}.
}
\label{eq:actual_Tstar}
\end{equation}

Then the exact reduced transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta_X I_\theta\,T_E,
\qquad
\beta=\beta_X I_\theta\,T_O,
}
\label{eq:actual_ab_master}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:actual_Itheta}
\end{equation}

So explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\beta_X\,T_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\beta_X\,T_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:actual_ab_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)
\iff
R_\perp>0.
}
\label{eq:actual_trans_nondeg}
\end{equation}

At the explicit folded-Bragg Class II level, the transverse derivative bookkeeping compresses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:actual_TII}
\end{equation}
and in the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto
iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\!\cdot\!G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:actual_TII_min}
\end{equation}

Therefore the strongest practical explicit transverse test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:actual_trans_test}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Full reduced symbol and full Dirac operator}

With
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
T_*=(T_E,T_O),
\]
the reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_XI_\theta T_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_XI_\theta T_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:actual_A1}
\end{equation}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) on the grade/valley factor.
Then the full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p).
}
\label{eq:actual_D1}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:actual_D1_explicit}
\end{align}

Its dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:actual_dispersion}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Strongest honest endpoint}

The remaining microscopic frontier is no longer theorem-level.
It is only the explicit finite insertion of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad
u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad
m_\parallel,\quad
T_E,\quad T_O.
}
\label{eq:actual_leftover}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, operationally, the final finite audit map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel,\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*))
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*,T_E,T_O)
\longmapsto
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:actual_final_map}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The strongest honest current coefficient sheet is already reduced to explicit finite projected matrix entries.

The longitudinal Bloch-overlap scalar is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}

The strongest practical sufficient condition is

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify

The transverse coefficients are

with

Hence the full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator is

+

with dispersion
\[

=

+

Therefore the remaining microscopic frontier is no longer structural.
It is only the literal finite insertion of

Equivalently, the final finite audit map is

\longmapsto

\section{Actual Projected-Matrix Coefficient Sheet for the Full Dirac Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the coefficient problem is no longer structural.
It is a literal finite projected-matrix audit.

The longitudinal side is reduced to the finite extraction of
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
while the transverse side is reduced to the explicit projected traces of
\[
M_1,\qquad M_2,
\]
or equivalently to the branch-level reduced coefficients
\[
A_E+B_E,\qquad A_O+B_O.
\]

\section{1. Valley-diagonal projected matrices}

Write the two \(2\times2\) valley-diagonal projected matrices as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:sheet_Epm}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

The low eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
}
\label{eq:sheet_epslow}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
}
\label{eq:sheet_rpm}
\end{equation}
Then the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:sheet_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:sheet_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

So the first longitudinal finite audit is exactly the insertion of
\[
a_\pm,\qquad b_\pm,\qquad c_\pm.
\]

\section{2. Reduced shell-normal \(J\)-matrix}

Define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:sheet_Upar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\label{eq:sheet_upar}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:sheet_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\label{eq:sheet_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

So the second longitudinal finite audit is exactly the insertion of
\[
u_{11},\qquad u_{22},\qquad m_\parallel.
\]

\section{3. Exact Branch-B longitudinal coefficient}

At exact Branch B level, the current shell-reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.

\label{eq:sheet_lambda_exact}

Using the explicit defect overlap value
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3

\section{4. Exact transverse projected-trace formulas}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\label{eq:sheet_Mi}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\label{eq:sheet_lambda_trace}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\label{eq:sheet_ab_trace}
\end{equation}

So, at exact projected-matrix level, the transverse finite audit is simply the explicit insertion of the two \(2\times2\) matrices
\[
M_1,\qquad M_2.
\]

\section{5. Current explicit branch-level transverse summary}

Inside the current explicit LO/Class II realization, the reduced transverse branch summary is
\begin{equation}

e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O),

and since
\[
\alpha=I_\theta e_0^{(1)},

one gets

=

\qquad

=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:sheet_ab_branch}
\end{equation}

Thus the current branch-level transverse finite audit is reduced to the insertion of
\[
A_E+B_E,
\qquad
A_O+B_O.
\]

Therefore the full Dirac architecture is no longer open.

\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

Therefore the only genuinely remaining microscopic frontier is the literal finite insertion of
\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel,\ A_E+B_E,\ A_O+B_O.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel,M_1,M_2)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*,\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
}
\]
is now the final finite audit map.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit First-Shell Bloch Ansatz and Matrix Element Evaluation}

\section{1. First-shell Bloch truncation}

Fix the enriched carrier basis
\[
|+,a\rangle = e^{iG_* \cdot x}\chi_a,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle = e^{-iG_* \cdot x}\chi_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\]

We adopt the minimal first-shell truncation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(x)
=
\sum_{a=1}^2
\left(
A_a^{(+)} e^{iG_*\cdot x}
+
A_a^{(-)} e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
\right)\chi_a.
}
\label{eq:ansatz_min}
\end{equation}

No higher harmonics are kept.

\section{2. Effective quadratic Hamiltonian projection}

The microscopic PDE gives quadratic form
\[
\mathcal H_{\text{eff}}
=
-\mu^2 + Z\nabla^2 - Y\nabla^4 + V_{\text{defect}}(x),
\]

Project onto the basis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_\pm(0))_{ab}
=
\langle \pm,a | \mathcal H_{\text{eff}} | \pm,b \rangle.
}
\label{eq:Epm_def}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Diagonal entries}

Using
\[
\nabla^2 e^{\pm iG_*x} = -G_*^2 e^{\pm iG_*x},
\qquad
\nabla^4 e^{\pm iG_*x} = G_*^4 e^{\pm iG_*x},
\]

we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\pm = b_\pm
=
-\mu^2 - ZG_*^2 - YG_*^4 + V_{00},
}
\label{eq:diag_entries}
\end{equation}
where
\[
V_{00} = \int d^3x\, V_{\text{defect}}(x).
\]

Thus diagonal asymmetry vanishes at this level:
\[
a_\pm = b_\pm.
\]

\section{4. Off-diagonal entries}

Off-diagonal mixing comes from defect Fourier mode at \(2G_*\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\pm
=
\int d^3x\, e^{-iG_*x} V_{\text{defect}}(x) e^{iG_*x}
=
\widehat V(2G_*).
}
\label{eq:c_entries}
\end{equation}

Thus
\[
c_+ = c_- = \widehat V(2G_*).
\]

\section{5. Resulting \(E_\pm(0)\)}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\epsilon_0 & c \\
\overline c & \epsilon_0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\epsilon_0 = -\mu^2 - ZG_*^2 - YG_*^4 + V_{00}.
}
\label{eq:Epm_final}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Eigenvectors and \(\Delta_{00}\)}

Eigenvalues:
\[
\epsilon_\pm = \epsilon_0 \mp |c|.
\]

Eigenvectors give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{|c|}{\sqrt{\epsilon_0^2 + |c|^2}}.
}
\label{eq:Delta00_result}
\end{equation}

Thus
\[
\Delta_{00} \neq 0 \iff c \neq 0.
\]

\section{7. Intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel^{ab}
=
\langle -,a | J_\parallel | +,b \rangle.
}
\end{equation}

Using plane waves:
\[
e^{-iG_*x} J(x) e^{iG_*x} \rightarrow \widehat J(2G_*),
\]

we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{11}-u_{22}
=
\widehat J_{11}(2G_*) - \widehat J_{22}(2G_*).
}
\label{eq:u_diff}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_* = \frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\left(
\widehat J_{11}(2G_*) - \widehat J_{22}(2G_*)
\right).
}
\label{eq:Lstar_final}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Longitudinal coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}
\alpha_X m_\parallel
\left(
\widehat J_{11}(2G_*) - \widehat J_{22}(2G_*)
\right)
\theta_0^3 \kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_numeric}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Transverse coefficients}

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_E+B_E \propto \widehat K_1(2G_*),
\qquad
A_O+B_O \propto \widehat K_2(2G_*).
}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,\widehat K_1(2G_*),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,\widehat K_2(2G_*).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_final}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Numerical Coefficient Extraction for a Tanh Defect}

\section{1. Defect profile}

Fix the standard domain-wall profile
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta(\xi) = \theta_0 \tanh(\kappa \xi).
}
\label{eq:tanh_profile}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)
=
\theta_0 \kappa \,\text{sech}^2(\kappa \xi).
}
\label{eq:tanh_derivative}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Fourier transform of defect core}

We need Fourier modes at momentum \(q=2G_*\).

Key integral:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi \, e^{-iq\xi} \,\text{sech}^2(\kappa \xi)
=
\frac{\pi q}{\kappa^2} \frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:sech2_fourier}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\theta'}(q)
=
\theta_0 \kappa
\cdot
\frac{\pi q}{\kappa^2}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}
=
\theta_0
\frac{\pi q}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:theta_prime_ft}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Longitudinal kernel}

The longitudinal coefficient depends on cubic overlap:
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3 = \theta_0^3 \kappa^3 \text{sech}^6(\kappa\xi).
\]

Fourier transform:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\int d\xi\, e^{-iq\xi}\text{sech}^6(\kappa\xi)
=
\frac{\pi q}{8\kappa^2}
\frac{(q^2 + 4\kappa^2)}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:sech6_ft}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\theta'^3}(q)
=
\theta_0^3 \kappa^3
\cdot
\frac{\pi q}{8\kappa^2}
\frac{(q^2 + 4\kappa^2)}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:theta3_ft}
\end{equation}

Evaluate at \(q=2G_*\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\theta'^3}(2G_*)
=
\theta_0^3 \kappa
\frac{\pi (2G_*)}{8}
\frac{(4G_*^2 + 4\kappa^2)}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:theta3_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Longitudinal coefficient}

Recall
\[
\lambda_\parallel \propto \widehat{\theta'^3}(2G_*) \cdot (\widehat J_{11}-\widehat J_{22}).
\]

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_\parallel
\cdot
\theta_0^3 \kappa
\frac{\pi G_* (G_*^2 + \kappa^2)}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}
\cdot
\left(
\widehat J_{11}(2G_*) - \widehat J_{22}(2G_*)
\right),
}
\label{eq:lambda_numeric}
\end{equation}
with
\[
C_\parallel = \frac{\alpha_X}{4}.
\]

\section{5. Transverse coefficients}

Similarly, transverse comes from linear \(\theta\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\theta}(q)
=
\theta_0
\frac{\pi}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi q}{2\kappa}\right)}.
}
\label{eq:theta_ft}
\end{equation}

Thus at \(q=2G_*\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\theta}(2G_*)
=
\theta_0
\frac{\pi}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_T
\cdot
\theta_0
\frac{\pi}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}
\cdot
\widehat K_1(2G_*),
}
\label{eq:alpha_numeric}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
C_T
\cdot
\theta_0
\frac{\pi}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}
\cdot
\widehat K_2(2G_*),
}
\label{eq:beta_numeric}
\end{equation}

with
\[
C_T = \frac{\beta_X}{2}.
\]

\section{6. Final scaling laws}

Thus the full Dirac coefficients scale as

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \sim
\theta_0^3 \kappa
\frac{G_*^3}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)},
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha,\beta \sim
\theta_0
\frac{1}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh\left(\frac{\pi G_*}{\kappa}\right)}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Regime analysis}

\subsection{Thin wall: \(\kappa \gg G_*\)}

\[
\sinh(x)\approx x
\Rightarrow
\lambda_\parallel \sim \theta_0^3 \kappa^2 G_*^2
\]

\subsection{Thick wall: \(\kappa \ll G_*\)}

\[
\sinh(x)\sim e^{x}
\Rightarrow
\lambda_\parallel \sim e^{-\pi G_*/\kappa}
\]

Thus Dirac fermion is exponentially suppressed for wide defects.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Numerical Evaluation of Dirac Coefficients (Canonical Unit Case)}

\section{1. Parameters}

We set
\[
G_* = 1,\quad \kappa = 1,\quad \theta_0 = 1,
\]
\[
\alpha_X = \beta_X = 1,
\]
\[
\widehat J_{11}-\widehat J_{22} = 1,\quad
\widehat K_1 = 1,\quad
\widehat K_2 = 1.
\]

\section{2. Useful number}

\[
\sinh(\pi) \approx 11.5487
\]

\section{3. Longitudinal coefficient}

From
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{4}
\cdot
\theta_0^3 \kappa
\cdot
\frac{\pi G_* (G_*^2+\kappa^2)}{\sinh(\pi G_*/\kappa)}
\cdot
(\widehat J_{11}-\widehat J_{22}),
\]

we get

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{1}{4}
\cdot
\frac{\pi \cdot 1 \cdot (1+1)}{11.5487}
\]

\[
=
\frac{1}{4} \cdot \frac{2\pi}{11.5487}
\]

\[
=
\frac{1}{4} \cdot 0.544
\approx 0.136
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \approx 0.136
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Transverse coefficients}

From
\[
\alpha
=
\frac{\beta_X}{2}
\cdot
\theta_0
\frac{\pi}{\kappa}
\frac{1}{\sinh(\pi G_*/\kappa)}
\cdot
\widehat K_1,
\]

we get

\[
\alpha
=
\frac{1}{2}
\cdot
\frac{\pi}{11.5487}
\approx
\frac{1}{2}\cdot 0.272
\approx 0.136
\]

Similarly,
\[
\beta \approx 0.136
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha \approx 0.136,
\qquad
\beta \approx 0.136
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Final Dirac operator}

\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
0.136\, p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(0.136 p_1 - 0.136 p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(0.136 p_2 + 0.136 p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2
\]

\section{6. Dispersion}

\[
E(p)^2
=
0.136^2\, p_\parallel^2
+
2\cdot 0.136^2 (p_1^2+p_2^2)
\]

\[
=
0.0185\, p_\parallel^2
+
0.0370 (p_1^2+p_2^2)
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)
=
\sqrt{
0.0185\, p_\parallel^2
+
0.0370 (p_1^2+p_2^2)
}
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Refined-Locked Truncation Ansatz for the Final Coefficient Sheet}

\section{Short explanation}

The uploaded notes already reduce the remaining carrier-side problem to the explicit finite extraction of:
\[
E_+(0),\qquad E_-(0),\qquad \hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),\qquad m_\parallel,
\]
for the longitudinal slot, and to the projected transverse traces (or equivalently the branch-level pair \(A_E+B_E,\ A_O+B_O\)) for the transverse slot.

So the correct next move is to choose the smallest symmetry-compatible \(2\times2\) ansatz for these projected matrices and write the coefficient sheet in closed finite form.

\section{1. Minimal Hermitian ansatz for the valley blocks}

Write the two projected valley-diagonal blocks in the standard Hermitian form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)
=
\varepsilon_\pm \mathbf 1_2
+
\delta_\pm \Sigma_3
+
\Re(c_\pm)\Sigma_1
-
\Im(c_\pm)\Sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Epm_pauli}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\varepsilon_\pm+\delta_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & \varepsilon_\pm-\delta_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\varepsilon_\pm,\delta_\pm\in\mathbb R,\quad c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Epm_matrix}
\end{equation}

This is the most general \(2\times2\) Hermitian projected ansatz and therefore the correct minimal input for the final longitudinal audit.

\section{2. Low eigenvectors and \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

The low eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\varepsilon_\pm
-
\sqrt{\delta_\pm^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_epslow}
\end{equation}

Define the standard ratio parameter
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{\delta_\pm+\sqrt{\delta_\pm^2+|c_\pm|^2}}.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_rpm}
\end{equation}

Then the normalized low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

So the Bloch-overlap part of the longitudinal audit is reduced completely to
\[
(\delta_+,c_+;\delta_-,c_-).
\]

\section{3. Minimal ansatz for the shell-normal intervalley block}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
u_0\,\mathbf 1_2
+
u_3\,\Sigma_3
+
u_1\,\Sigma_1
+
u_2\,\Sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Upar_pauli}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_0+u_3 & u_1-i u_2\\
u_1+i u_2 & u_0-u_3
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_0,u_1,u_2,u_3\in\mathbb R.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Upar_matrix}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
u_3
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_upar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the unresolved longitudinal invariant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
m_\parallel u_3
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_3=0.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Lstar_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Longitudinal coefficient in closed finite form}

The exact Branch-B longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_lambda_master}
\end{equation}

Using the already evaluated defect overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:minansatz_I3}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_lambda_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_lambda_entries}
\end{equation}

The practical sufficient condition from the uploaded notes is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_long_practical}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
u_3\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_long_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Transverse coefficient ansatz}

On the transverse side, the exact projected trace formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_ab_trace}
\end{equation}

In the current explicit LO/Class II branch, the notes compress this to the reduced pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E:=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
T_O:=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
}
\label{eq:minansatz_TE_TO}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta T_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta T_O.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_ab_master}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:minansatz_Itheta}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
}
\label{eq:minansatz_alpha_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_beta_final}
\end{equation}

The transverse nondegeneracy condition is therefore simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(T_E,T_O)\neq(0,0)
\iff
(A_E+B_E,\ A_O+B_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_trans_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) on the grade/valley factor.
Then the reduced \(2\times2\) symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:minansatz_A1}
\end{equation}
and the full graded Dirac operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_D1}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:minansatz_D1_explicit}
\end{equation}

Its dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_dispersion}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest endpoint}

So the remaining coefficient-finding problem is now fully finite and explicit.

The longitudinal slot is completely reduced to
\[
\delta_\pm,\qquad c_\pm,\qquad u_3,\qquad m_\parallel,
\]
and the transverse slot is completely reduced to
\[
T_E,\qquad T_O
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
A_E+B_E,\qquad A_O+B_O.
\]

Equivalently, the final finite audit map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\delta_+,c_+;\ \delta_-,c_-;\ u_3;\ m_\parallel;\ T_E;\ T_O)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*,\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:minansatz_final_map}
\end{equation}

No new structural theorem is missing at this stage.

\section{Final Summary}

The strongest honest current coefficient sheet is already reduced to a finite projected-matrix ansatz.

The valley-diagonal blocks are
\[
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\varepsilon_\pm+\delta_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & \varepsilon_\pm-\delta_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
so the Bloch-overlap scalar is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}},
\qquad
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{\delta_\pm+\sqrt{\delta_\pm^2+|c_\pm|^2}}.
}
\]

The shell-normal intervalley block is
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_3\Sigma_3+u_1\Sigma_1+u_2\Sigma_2,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel=u_3=\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\]

Therefore the longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

The practical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,\qquad
u_3\neq0,\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\]

The transverse reduced coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\]

Hence the full graded Dirac operator is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
(\alpha p_2+\beta p_1)\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

Therefore the only genuinely remaining microscopic frontier is the literal finite insertion of
\[
\boxed{
\delta_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_3,\ m_\parallel,\ T_E,\ T_O.
}
\]

Equivalently, the final finite audit map is
\[
\boxed{
(\delta_+,c_+;\ \delta_-,c_-;\ u_3;\ m_\parallel;\ T_E;\ T_O)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*,\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Pure-Even Refined-Locked Closure Ansatz}

\section{Short explanation}

We choose the smallest symmetry-compatible ansatz that closes the remaining projected-matrix insertion problem.

The goal is not to claim that the microscopic values are uniquely fixed by the uploaded formulas alone.
The goal is to reduce the remaining finite audit to the smallest explicit parameter sheet consistent with the exact formulas already established.

\section{1. Minimal pure-even ansatz for the valley blocks}

Take the two projected valley-diagonal blocks to have the same internal orientation but possibly different scalar shifts:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+(0)=\varepsilon_+\mathbf 1_2+\delta\,\Sigma_3+c\,\Sigma_1,
\qquad
E_-(0)=\varepsilon_-\mathbf 1_2+\delta\,\Sigma_3+c\,\Sigma_1,
}
\label{eq:minclose_Epm}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\varepsilon_\pm,\delta,c\in\mathbb R.
\]

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\varepsilon_\pm+\delta & c\\
c & \varepsilon_\pm-\delta
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Epm_matrix}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal real-Hermitian ansatz compatible with the remaining finite longitudinal audit.

\section{2. Explicit \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

For \eqref{eq:minclose_Epm}, the low eigenvalue of each block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\varepsilon_\pm-\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}.
}
\label{eq:minclose_epslow}
\end{equation}

The ratio parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r
=
-\frac{c}{\delta+\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}.
}
\label{eq:minclose_r}
\end{equation}

Since both valley blocks have the same internal orientation in this minimal ansatz, one has \(r_+=r_-=r\), and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-r^2}{1+r^2}
=
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0
\iff
\delta\neq0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Delta00_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the Bloch-overlap part of the longitudinal audit is reduced to just the two real scalars
\[
\delta,\qquad c.
\]

\section{3. Minimal pure-even ansatz for the shell-normal \(J\)-block}

Take the shell-normal intervalley block to be diagonal in the same internal basis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel=u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_3\Sigma_3
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_0+u_3 & 0\\
0 & u_0-u_3
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_0,u_3\in\mathbb R.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Upar}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)=u_3,
}
\label{eq:minclose_upar}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq0
\iff
m_\parallel\neq0
\quad\text{and}\quad
u_3\neq0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_Lstar_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Longitudinal coefficient}

The exact Branch-B longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:minclose_lambda_master}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:minclose_I3}
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:minclose_lambda}
\end{equation}

Under first-shell dominant intervalley compression, the practical sufficient condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,A_{G_*}
\right|
>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:minclose_long_suff}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), this collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_3\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_long_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Minimal pure-even transverse ansatz}

For the pure-even branch we set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_O=0,
\qquad
T_E=:T\neq0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_TE}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta T,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_ab_master}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:minclose_Itheta}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_ab}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the LO/Class II branch summary where
\[
T_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\]
one may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_ab_branch}
\end{equation}

Thus the transverse slot is reduced to one real scalar:
\[
T
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
A_E+B_E.
\]

\section{6. Completed reduced symbol}

Under the minimal pure-even closure ansatz, the reduced symbol becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:minclose_A1}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T.
\]

\section{7. Full \(4\times4\) graded Dirac operator}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) on the grade/valley factor.
Then the full graded Dirac operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:minclose_D1}
\end{equation}

Its dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+\alpha^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:minclose_disp}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Final minimal coefficient sheet}

So the minimal pure-even refined-locked coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_3,
}
\label{eq:minclose_sheet1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:minclose_sheet2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:minclose_sheet3}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire remaining microscopic frontier is reduced to the finite real parameter set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta,\qquad c,\qquad u_3,\qquad m_\parallel,\qquad T.
}
\label{eq:minclose_sheet4}
\end{equation}
No further structural theorem is missing.

\section{Final Summary}

Under the minimal pure-even refined-locked closure ansatz,
\[
E_\pm(0)=\varepsilon_\pm\mathbf 1_2+\delta\,\Sigma_3+c\,\Sigma_1,
\qquad
U_\parallel=u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
T_O=0,\quad T_E=T.
\]

Then the Bloch-overlap scalar is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}.
}
\]

The shell-normal longitudinal invariant is
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\]

Therefore the longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

The pure-even transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\]

Hence the full graded Dirac operator is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\]

The practical sufficient longitudinal condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_3\,A_{G_*}
\right|
>|R_N|.
}
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is reduced to the finite real parameter set
\[
\boxed{
\delta,\qquad c,\qquad u_3,\qquad m_\parallel,\qquad T.
}
\]
No additional structural theorem is missing.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Canonical Order-One Evaluation of the Coefficient Sheet}

\section{1. Canonical parameter choice}

We choose the minimal order-one canonical insertion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta = c = u_3 = m_\parallel = T = 1,
\qquad
\alpha_X = 1,
\qquad
A_{G_*}=1.
}
\end{equation}

This corresponds to a generic non-fine-tuned microscopic configuration.

\section{2. Bloch-overlap scalar}

\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}.
\end{equation}

So the overlap is order-one:
\[
\boxed{\Delta_{00}\sim O(1)}
\]

\section{3. Longitudinal coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}
\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
C_\parallel := \frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}.
\end{equation}

Numerically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel \approx 0.0319.
}
\end{equation}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \approx -0.032\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Transverse coefficient}

\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
C_\perp := \frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}.
\end{equation}

Numerically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\perp \approx 0.340.
}
\end{equation}

Thus:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha \approx -0.34\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Anisotropy ratio}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
:=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha}.
}
\end{equation}

Then:
\begin{equation}
\rho
=
\frac{C_\parallel}{C_\perp}
\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\end{equation}

Compute the constant:
\begin{equation}
\frac{C_\parallel}{C_\perp}
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi/512}{\sqrt3\pi/16}
=
\frac{3}{32}.
\end{equation}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final dispersion}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
\alpha^2 (p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Key scaling result}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \sim \theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha \sim \theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\rho \sim \theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Under the canonical order-one insertion,
\[
\delta=c=u_3=m_\parallel=T=\alpha_X=A_{G_*}=1,
\]
we obtain:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \approx -0.032\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\alpha \approx -0.34\,\theta_0\kappa
}
\]

The anisotropy ratio is
\[
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\]

Therefore,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel \ll \alpha
\quad \text{for small } \theta_0\kappa,
}
\]

and longitudinal transport is parametrically suppressed.

The emergent Dirac dispersion is
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
\alpha^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Pure-Even Refined-Locked Coefficient Sheet up to the Anisotropy Ratio}

\section{Short explanation}

At the current strongest honest stage, the carrier-side problem is already reduced to finite projected data.

The longitudinal side is governed by
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
while the transverse side is governed by the pure-even scalar
\[
T_E=:T,
\qquad
T_O=0.
\]

Therefore the full reduced coefficient sheet and the anisotropy ratio \(\rho\) can be written in closed finite form.

\section{1. Minimal pure-even projected ansatz}

Take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm(0)
=
\varepsilon_\pm \mathbf 1_2+\delta\,\Sigma_3+c\,\Sigma_1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_\pm,\delta,c\in\mathbb R,
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Epm}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
u_0,u_3\in\mathbb R.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Upar}
\end{equation}

On the transverse side, impose the minimal pure-even closure
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_O=0,
\qquad
T_E=:T.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_TE}
\end{equation}

This is the smallest symmetry-compatible closure ansatz consistent with the exact formulas already isolated in the uploaded notes.

\section{2. Explicit longitudinal overlap scalar}

For \eqref{eq:rhoans_Epm}, the low eigenvectors of the two valley blocks have the same internal orientation, so the Bloch-overlap scalar becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0
\iff
\delta\neq0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Delta00_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire overlap part of the longitudinal audit is reduced to the two real scalars \(\delta,c\).

\section{3. Explicit longitudinal invariant}

From \eqref{eq:rhoans_Upar},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
u_3.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_upar}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
m_\parallel u_3.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq0
\iff
m_\parallel\neq0
\quad\text{and}\quad
u_3\neq0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Lstar_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Longitudinal coefficient}

The exact Branch-B longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_lambda_master}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:rhoans_I3}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_3\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_lambda}
\end{equation}

The practical sufficient longitudinal condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_3\,A_{G_*}
\right|
>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_long_suff}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_3\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_long_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Transverse coefficients}

For the pure-even branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta T,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ab_master}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:rhoans_Itheta}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ab}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the LO/Class-II branch summary where
\[
T=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\]
one may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ab_branch}
\end{equation}

Thus transverse survival is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T\neq0
\iff
A_E+B_E\neq0.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_trans_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact anisotropy ratio}

Since \(\beta=0\), the transverse speed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}=|\alpha|=\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}|\theta_0\kappa T|.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_vperp}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{|\alpha|}
=
\frac{
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
}{
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}|\theta_0\kappa T|
}.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ratio_raw}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_3}{|T|}\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\cdot
\operatorname{sgn}(T).
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ratio_signed}
\end{equation}

At the level of magnitude,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_ratio_abs}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the minimal pure-even realization of the general anisotropy law already isolated in the uploaded notes.

\section{7. Regimes}

The longitudinal and transverse coefficients scale as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\sim \theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha\sim \theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:rhoans_scaling}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim (\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_scaling_rho}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll1
\quad\text{for}\quad
|\theta_0\kappa|\ll1,
}
\label{eq:rhoans_small}
\end{equation}
which is the natural strongly anisotropic Branch-B regime emphasized in the notes, while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim1
}
\label{eq:rhoans_order1}
\end{equation}
requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}\,
\frac{|T|}{|\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3|}.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_iso_window}
\end{equation}

So isotropy is not generic in this minimal branch; it requires a parametric enhancement of the longitudinal invariant relative to the transverse one.

\section{8. Completed reduced symbol and full Dirac operator}

The reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:rhoans_A1}
\end{equation}

Introduce Pauli matrices \(\rho_a\) on the grading/valley factor.
Then the full graded Dirac operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\rho_1\otimes A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_3
+
\alpha p_1\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_1
+
\alpha p_2\,\rho_1\otimes\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_D1}
\end{equation}

Its dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
\alpha^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:rhoans_dispersion}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Honest endpoint}

Under the minimal pure-even refined-locked closure ansatz, the entire remaining microscopic frontier is reduced to the finite real parameter set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta,\qquad c,\qquad u_3,\qquad m_\parallel,\qquad T.
}
\label{eq:rhoans_leftover}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\delta,c,u_3,m_\parallel,T)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*,\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\rho).
}
\label{eq:rhoans_final_map}
\end{equation}

No new structural theorem is missing at this stage.

\section{Final Summary}

Under the minimal pure-even refined-locked closure ansatz
\[
E_\pm(0)=\varepsilon_\pm\mathbf 1_2+\delta\Sigma_3+c\Sigma_1,
\qquad
U_\parallel=u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_3\Sigma_3,
\qquad
T_O=0,\quad T_E=T,
\]
the Bloch-overlap scalar is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}.
}
\]

The longitudinal invariant is
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_3.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,T,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\]

Hence the anisotropy ratio is
\[
\boxed{
\rho
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_3}{|T|}\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\cdot
\operatorname{sgn}(T),
}
\]
or in magnitude
\[
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

Thus the natural regime of this minimal branch is
\[
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll1
\quad\text{when}\quad
|\theta_0\kappa|\ll1,
}
\]
while \( |\rho|\sim1 \) requires the parameter balance
\[
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}\,
\frac{|T|}{|\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3|}.
}
\]

The practical sufficient longitudinal condition is
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\delta}{\sqrt{\delta^2+c^2}}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_3\,A_{G_*}
\right|
>|R_N|.
}
\]

Therefore the entire remaining microscopic frontier has been reduced to the five real parameters
\[
\boxed{
\delta,\qquad c,\qquad u_3,\qquad m_\parallel,\qquad T.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Isotropy Window from the Minimal Pure-Even Coefficient Sheet}

\section{1. Starting point}

We start from the exact reduced anisotropy law:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:iso_rho}
\end{equation}

Define the dimensionless control parameter
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{C}
:=
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}.
}
\label{eq:iso_C}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\mathcal{C}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:iso_rho_C}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact isotropy condition}

Isotropy corresponds to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim1.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{3}{32}\,
\mathcal{C}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim 1.
}
\label{eq:iso_condition}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}\,
\frac{1}{\mathcal{C}}.
}
\label{eq:iso_theta}
\end{equation}

Substituting back:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}\,
\frac{|T|}{|\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3|}.
}
\label{eq:iso_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Necessary and sufficient inequality form}

Define an \(\epsilon\)-window for approximate isotropy:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{1}{K}
\le
|\rho|
\le
K,
\qquad
K=O(1).
}
\end{equation}

Then using \eqref{eq:iso_rho_C}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{32}{3K}
\le
\mathcal{C}\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\le
\frac{32K}{3}.
}
\label{eq:iso_band}
\end{equation}

Thus the isotropy window is exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{32}{3K}
\le
|\alpha_X|\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\le
\frac{32K}{3}.
}
\label{eq:iso_full_band}
\end{equation}

This is a necessary and sufficient condition.

\section{4. Regime classification}

From \eqref{eq:iso_rho_C}:

\subsection{(i) Strong anisotropy regime}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{C}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 \ll 1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\rho|\ll1.
}
\end{equation}

This is the natural regime for small defects.

\subsection{(ii) Isotropic window}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{C}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 \sim O(1)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\rho|\sim1.
}
\end{equation}

This requires a balance:
\[
(\theta_0\kappa)^2 \sim \frac{1}{\mathcal{C}}.
\]

\subsection{(iii) Longitudinal-dominant regime}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{C}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 \gg 1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\rho|\gg1.
}
\end{equation}

This corresponds to over-enhanced longitudinal transport.

\section{5. Non-genericity of isotropy}

Generically,
\[
\mathcal{C}=O(1),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|
\sim
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\end{equation}

Thus for small defects:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll1,
}
\end{equation}
and isotropy requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\theta_0\kappa)^2=O(1),
}
\end{equation}
or a compensating enhancement in
\[
\frac{m_\parallel u_3}{T}.
\]

\section{6. Structural conclusion}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Isotropy is not generic in the minimal pure-even Branch-B.}
}
\end{equation}

It requires a tuned balance between:

\begin{itemize}
\item defect strength \((\theta_0\kappa)\),
\item longitudinal invariant \(m_\parallel u_3\),
\item transverse amplitude \(T\).
\end{itemize}

\section{7. Final closed statement}

The exact necessary and sufficient isotropy condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim1
\iff
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}
\frac{|T|}{|\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3|}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The reduced anisotropy law is
\[
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

Define
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal{C}
=
|\alpha_X|\,
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
|\rho|
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\mathcal{C}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

The exact isotropy condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim1
\iff
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\sim
\frac{32}{3}
\frac{|T|}{|\alpha_X m_\parallel u_3|}.
}
\]

The necessary and sufficient inequality form is
\[
\boxed{
\frac{32}{3K}
\le
|\alpha_X|
\frac{|m_\parallel u_3|}{|T|}
(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\le
\frac{32K}{3}.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
|\rho|\ll1 \text{ (generic, small defect)}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\rho|\sim1 \text{ (fine-tuned isotropic window)}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\rho|\gg1 \text{ (longitudinal-dominant regime)}
}
\]

Thus isotropy is not generic in the minimal pure-even Branch-B, but arises only from a parameter balance.
